< review>
Arco tends to be cheaper than most gas stations. This one is generally cheaper than the other big brands in the surrounding area.
Is a touch run down with graffiti here and there.
New card reader model in the pumps, so quick using a debit card.... But $0.35 card use fee added each time. Else, bring cash and go inside.
Arco's don't take credit to reduce the price for gas, but can result in headaches having to go to the bank first for cash if you want to avoid the card fee.
Access can be easy heading south towards the freeway, but requires a left turn at the light going North from the freeway. The light has a sign that says no u-turn, forcing you to make a left at the light, then another to enter the station.
Pump filled quickly without notice delay, stopped near the tank full capacity as expected without going over.< /review>

I decided to try out Cornerstone one day a couple of years ago because I had driven by it on the freeway for so many years. I did not know what to expect, other than what I had seen on their website about service times and where it was. The worship was contemporary and fun, and the sermon and pastor were both wonderful. All of the pastors teach from the Bible and have all of the readings from the sermon in our notes, to read along with, highlight and write notes on. The sermon notes also include a fill-in-the-blank type study to follow along with, which reinforces the principles that we just read about, and it really helps me to connect to what I'm reading. In addition, the pastors are the perfect balance of funny, energetic and reverent, which is even better than I had hoped for when I was trying out the church. Everyone at Cornerstone is so friendly, from the moment you get out of your car and every step of the way. I am so happy to say that after 5 years of "church-hopping" looking for the "right" church for me, I found not only that at Cornerstone, but I found a family too. The Bible study groups and ministry departments are such a blessing and I can't recommend this church enough if you live in the area.< /Review>

<username>Amanda Root< /username><Time>1552862905920<//Time><rating>5</rating>< review>
I live in Washington now, but this market makes me wish I moved back to Pasadena!

We didn‚Äôt have troubles parking, however we arrived around 11:30 so the amount of people was slowing down a bit. This is an early market with some people selling out before they close so I would suggest visiting earlier!

The vendors and quality that everyone brings is some of the best I‚Äôve ever seen!!

You will find the freshest of produce, flowers, and bulk items like nuts, dried fruits, honeys and marmalade‚Äôs, sweet treats and savory.

Most vendors seemed to be cash only although some took card. I didn‚Äôt have any cash and I‚Äôm on vacation and not doing much cooking so I didn‚Äôt get to take home any of the incredible produce, but if I lived here this would likely be my primary source of produce for my household!

My friend and I did buy some incredible dried cherries, apples, honey roasted almonds and jalape√±o stuffed green olives from one vendor. We also got baked tapioca from another. I wish I knew the name of this vendor because that baked tapioca was one of the best treats I‚Äôve ever had!! Not too sweet but light and fluffy. Ugh, I‚Äôm drooling!

This market is so lovely and I‚Äôm envious of the residents who get to experience it every Saturday!< /review>

<user_id>116634455223274139400<//user_id><name>Teresa Vasievich< /name><date>1547440545576</date><Rate>3</Rate>< review>
When I initially walked into the Dental Suite, I had a great first impression. The lobby was beautiful and the receptionist had all of my paperwork ready to go on a clipboard with a little sign that said "Welcome Teresa!" - a great personal touch. The receptionist personally introduced herself and was very kind. I filled out the necessary paperwork, as it was my first time at this office, and waited for the dental tech to call my name. Once they were ready for me, the tech didn't even call my name. I just saw her motion to the receptionist and ask if I was ready, which I found rather rude since I was sitting right there.

Then she took me back to get initial x-rays. There were no introductions. There was no "you can set your coat here and your bag there." There wasn't even an introduction to what she was doing. I just sat on the chair and immediately she was putting the x-ray shield on me. It was a very cold start. Then she proceeded to take, what I believe to be, way too many x-rays of my teeth. There were probably 20 or so pictures taken because so many needed to be done twice or three times for her to get a "good" picture. The whole process took about 40 minutes - way too long in my book.

Once Dr. Rostker got to me I felt like I knew more of what was going on. She went through the x-rays with me and explained what she was seeing. She was writing notes as we went which made me feel more comfortable that when she went back to look at my chart later, she would remember what we discussed. Then she proceeded to do my cleaning and asked if I wanted to watch Netflix while she worked - so nice! Dr. Rostker was great, but to be honest I'm nervous about returning if all of her staff is unsure and obviously nervous about their jobs.< /review>

< review>
I have been going to this awesome store for at least 30 years!  It changed hands 20 years ago and is STILL going strong!  How does a small hobby shop stay in business competing with the internet?  It is with AWESOME service, products and friendly, knowledgeable staff!  The Train Crossing is a family business and the owners all take pride in carrying on the family tradition.  This is my go to place for scratch building supplies and tools.  If they don't have something in stock, they WILL get it for you.  They have a dizzying array of trains, rolling stock and model landscaping supplies.  Check 'em out!</review>

< Review>
Those is a great place for a quick bite alone or with friends. It is also an excellent place to sit and work. The atmosphere is pleasant. It is generally clean, quiet, and welcoming. There is some unusual artwork on the walls which works well. Outside seating is also an option.

The personal pizzas are a must try. The salads are decent too. It is definitely vegetarian friendly.

What makes this place excellent is the variety of (non-alcoholic) drink options. The ginger lemonade is highly recommended (it is quite ginger-y). The golden latte is delicious.</Review>

The perfect all-around caf√©. If there's one place I'll miss after leaving SF, it's's Atlas. Grab a beer, a coffee, breakfast, lunch or dinner, indoors, outdoors, sit there for a few hours, just pop in for a second, hear some live music, you can do it all here

Been here a few times. The food and coffee is good -- I really loved the beet salad. The ambiance is kind of meh -- every other minute the staff shout the order numbers that are ready at the top of their lungs. < review>
Came here because I saw it on 'Senses 8', a programme on Netflix. It was a lovely setting with wifi for 2 hours, indoor and outdoor seating. Food looked delicious and was around $10 mark. The staff were friendly and helpful. Tea range is great, coffee is fab and they have alcoholic drinks (beer, wine) and one of the biggest ranges of kombucha- they do a delicious green tea kombucha! Would recommend to go here for either catch up with your friends or studying! Has been around for 20 years so well established and knows what's up.<//review>
